<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Dance</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Performing art consisting of movement of the body</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Dance_(disambiguation)" title="Dance (disambiguation)">Dance (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Two_dancers.jpg"><img alt="A man and woman, mid-leap" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="633" decoding="async" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Two_dancers.jpg/220px-Two_dancers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Two_dancers.jpg/330px-Two_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Two_dancers.jpg/440px-Two_dancers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Two_dancers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern dancers</a></div></div></div>

<p><b>Dance</b> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Performing_art" title="Performing art">performing art</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_form" title="Art form">form</a> consisting of sequences of movement, either improvised or purposefully selected. This movement has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aesthetic" title="Aesthetic">aesthetic</a> and often <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">symbolic</a> value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[nb 1]</a></sup> Dance can be categorized and described by its <a href="/wiki/Choreography" title="Choreography">choreography</a>, by its repertoire of movements, or by its <a href="/wiki/History_of_dance" title="History of dance">historical period</a> or <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic,_regional,_and_folk_dances_by_origin" title="List of ethnic, regional, and folk dances by origin">place of origin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>An important distinction is to be drawn between the contexts of <a href="/wiki/Concert_dance" title="Concert dance">theatrical</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Participation_dance" title="Participation dance">participatory</a> dance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> although these two categories are not always completely separate; both may have special functions, whether <a href="/wiki/Social_dance" title="Social dance">social</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_dance" title="Ceremonial dance">ceremonial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Competitive_dance" title="Competitive dance">competitive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erotic_dance" title="Erotic dance">erotic</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_dance" title="War dance">martial</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Sacred_dance" title="Sacred dance">sacred</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liturgical_dance" title="Liturgical dance">liturgical</a>. Other forms of human movement are sometimes said to have a dance-like quality, including <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skating</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synchronised_swimming" title="Synchronised swimming">synchronized swimming</a>, marching bands, and many other forms of <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(physical_culture)" title="Athletics (physical culture)">athletics</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_and_participation">Performance and participation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Performance and participation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GDC_onlywayaround.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="1012" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GDC_onlywayaround.jpg/300px-GDC_onlywayaround.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GDC_onlywayaround.jpg/450px-GDC_onlywayaround.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/GDC_onlywayaround.jpg/600px-GDC_onlywayaround.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GDC_onlywayaround.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of an American jazz dance company perform a formal group routine in a concert dance setting</div></div></div>
<p>Theatrical dance, also called performance or concert dance, is intended primarily as a spectacle, usually a <a href="/wiki/Performance" title="Performance">performance</a> upon a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stage_(theater)" title="Stage (theater)">stage</a> by <a href="/wiki/Virtuoso" title="Virtuoso">virtuoso</a> dancers. It often tells a <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">story</a>, perhaps using <a href="/wiki/Mime_artist" title="Mime artist">mime</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dance_costumes" title="Dance costumes">costume</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theatrical_scenery" title="Theatrical scenery">scenery</a>, or else it may simply <a href="/wiki/Interpretive_dance" title="Interpretive dance">interpret the musical accompaniment</a>, which is often specially composed and performed in a theatre setting but it is not a requirement. Examples are western <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern dance</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Indian_dance" title="Classical Indian dance">Classical Indian dance</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bharatanatyam" title="Bharatanatyam">Bharatanatyam</a> and Chinese and Japanese song and dance dramas such as <a href="/wiki/Dragon_dance" title="Dragon dance">dragon dance</a>. Most classical forms are centred upon dance alone, but performance dance may also appear in <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musical theatre</a>.
</p><p>Participatory dance, on the other hand, whether it be a <a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">folk dance</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Social_dance" title="Social dance">social dance</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Group_dance" title="Group dance">group dance</a> such as a <a href="/wiki/Line_dance" title="Line dance">line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circle_dance" title="Circle dance">circle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medieval_dance#Other_Chain_Dances" title="Medieval dance">chain</a> or <a href="/wiki/Square_dance" title="Square dance">square dance</a>, or a <a href="/wiki/Partner_dance" title="Partner dance">partner dance</a> such as is common in <a href="/wiki/Ballroom_dance" title="Ballroom dance">Western ballroom dancing</a>, is undertaken primarily for a common purpose, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_interaction" title="Social interaction">social interaction</a> or <a href="/wiki/Exercise" title="Exercise">exercise</a>, or building flexibility of participants rather than to serve any benefit to onlookers. Such dance seldom has any narrative. A group dance and a <i><a href="/wiki/Corps_de_ballet" title="Corps de ballet">corps de ballet</a></i>, a social partner dance and a <i><a href="/wiki/Pas_de_deux" title="Pas de deux">pas de deux</a></i>, differ profoundly. Even a <a href="/wiki/Solo_dance" title="Solo dance">solo dance</a> may be undertaken solely for the satisfaction of the dancer. Participatory dancers often all employ the same movements and steps but, for example, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rave_culture" title="Rave culture">rave culture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music</a>, vast crowds may engage in <a href="/wiki/Free_dance" title="Free dance">free dance</a>, uncoordinated with those around them. On the other hand, some cultures lay down strict rules as to the particular dances in which, for example, men, women, and children may or must participate.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_dance" title="History of dance">History of dance</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg/220px-Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg/330px-Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg/440px-Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_painting_at_Bhimbetka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mesolithic dancers at Bhimbetka</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archeology" title="Archeology">Archaeological</a> evidence for early dance includes 10,000-year-old paintings in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh,_India" title="Madhya Pradesh, India">Madhya Pradesh, India</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Shelters_of_Bhimbetka" title="Rock Shelters of Bhimbetka">Rock Shelters of Bhimbetka</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YM_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-YM-7">[6]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egyptian</a> tomb paintings depicting dancing figures, dated c. 3300 BC. It has been proposed that before the invention of written languages, dance was an important part of the oral and performance methods of passing stories down from one generation to the next.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lecomte_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-lecomte-8">[7]</a></sup> The use of dance in <a href="/wiki/Ecstasy_(emotion)" title="Ecstasy (emotion)">ecstatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Altered_state_of_consciousness" title="Altered state of consciousness">trance states</a> and healing rituals (as observed today in many contemporary "primitive" cultures, from the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>) is thought to have been another early factor in the social development of dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guenther_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-guenther-9">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>References to dance can be found in very early recorded history; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_dance" title="Greek dance">Greek dance</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horos" title="Horos">horos</a></i>) is referred to by <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucian" title="Lucian">Lucian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> and <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Talmud</a> refer to many events related to dance, and contain over 30 different dance terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Chinese_classical_dance" title="History of Chinese classical dance">Chinese</a> pottery as early as the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period, groups of people are depicted dancing in a line holding hands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> and the earliest Chinese word for "dance" is found written in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oracle_bones" title="Oracle bones">oracle bones</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> Dance is further described in the <i><a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshi_Chunqiu" title="Lüshi Chunqiu">Lüshi Chunqiu</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aesthetic_tradition_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-aesthetic_tradition-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Primitive dance in ancient China was associated with sorcery and shamanic rituals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg/180px-Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg/270px-Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg/360px-Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_Statuette_of_a_Veiled_and_Masked_Dancer_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greek bronze statuette of a veiled and masked dancer, 3rd–2nd century BC, Alexandria, Egypt</div></div></div>
<p>During the first millennium <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_era" title="Common era">BCE</a> in India, many texts were composed which attempted to codify aspects of daily life. <a href="/wiki/Bharata_Muni" title="Bharata Muni">Bharata Muni</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natyashastra" title="Natyashastra">Natyashastra</a></i> (literally <i>"the text of dramaturgy"</i>) is one of the earlier texts. It mainly deals with drama, in which dance plays an important part in Indian culture. It categorizes dance into four types--secular, ritual, abstract, and, interpretive--and into four regional varieties. The text elaborates various hand-gestures (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudras" title="Mudras">mudras</a></i>) and classifies movements of the various limbs, steps and so on. A strong continuous tradition of dance has since continued in India, through to modern times, where it continues to play a role in culture, ritual, and, notably, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> entertainment industry. Many other <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_dance" title="Contemporary dance">contemporary dance</a> forms can likewise be traced back to <a href="/wiki/Historical_dance" title="Historical dance">historical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_dance" title="Traditional dance">traditional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_dance" title="Ceremonial dance">ceremonial</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_dances_sorted_by_ethnicity" title="List of dances sorted by ethnicity">ethnic</a> dance.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">Dance music</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg/220px-Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg/330px-Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg/440px-Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_girls_in_concert.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two women dance at a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a> concert in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sofia,_Bulgaria" title="Sofia, Bulgaria">Sofia, Bulgaria</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Dance is generally, however not exclusively, performed with the accompaniment of music and may or may not be performed <i>in <a href="/wiki/Time_signature" title="Time signature">time</a></i> to such music. Some dance (such as <a href="/wiki/Tap_dance" title="Tap dance">tap dance</a>) may provide its own audible accompaniment in place of (or in addition to) music. Many early forms of music and dance were created for each other and are frequently performed together. Notable examples of traditional dance/music couplings include the <a href="/wiki/Jig" title="Jig">jig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tango_music" title="Tango music">tango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">salsa</a>. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musical_genre" title="Musical genre">musical genres</a> have a parallel dance form such as <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque_dance" title="Baroque dance">baroque dance</a>; other varieties of dance and music may share nomenclature but developed separately, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_music_era" title="Classical music era">classical music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_ballet" title="Classical ballet">classical ballet</a>. The choreography and music go hand in hand, as they complement each other to express a story told by the choreographer and or dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhythm">Rhythm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rhythm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">Rhythm</a> and dance are deeply linked in history and practice. The American dancer <a href="/wiki/Ted_Shawn" title="Ted Shawn">Ted Shawn</a> wrote; "The conception of rhythm which underlies all studies of the dance is something about which we could talk forever, and still not finish."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shawn_50_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shawn_50-18">[17]</a></sup> A musical rhythm requires two main elements; first, a regularly-repeating <a href="/wiki/Pulse_(music)" title="Pulse (music)">pulse</a> (also called the "beat" or "tactus") that establishes the <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> and, second, a pattern of <a href="/wiki/Accent_(music)" title="Accent (music)">accents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rest_(music)" title="Rest (music)">rests</a> that establishes the character of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meter_(music)" title="Meter (music)">metre or basic rhythmic pattern</a>. The basic pulse is roughly equal in duration to a simple step or gesture.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tango_rhythm.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="23" data-file-width="332" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tango_rhythm.svg/220px-Tango_rhythm.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tango_rhythm.svg/330px-Tango_rhythm.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tango_rhythm.svg/440px-Tango_rhythm.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tango_rhythm.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A basic tango rhythm</div></div></div>
<p>Dances generally have a characteristic tempo and rhythmic pattern. The tango, for example, is usually danced in <span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span style="font-family: 'Georgia Pro', Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', Times, 'Times New Roman', FreeSerif, 'DejaVu Math TeX', 'URW Bookman L', serif;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:0.85em;font-size:80%;text-align:center"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"><b>2</b></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"><b>4</b></sub></span></span></span> time at approximately 66 beats per minute. The basic slow step, called a "slow", lasts for one beat, so that a full "right–left" step is equal to one <span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span style="font-family: 'Georgia Pro', Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', Times, 'Times New Roman', FreeSerif, 'DejaVu Math TeX', 'URW Bookman L', serif;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:0.85em;font-size:80%;text-align:center"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"><b>2</b></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"><b>4</b></sub></span></span></span> measure. The basic forward and backward walk of the dance is so counted – "slow-slow" – while many additional figures are counted "slow – quick-quick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Just as musical rhythms (e.g., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drum_beats" title="Drum beats">drum beats</a>) are defined by a pattern of strong and weak beats, so repetitive body movements often depend on alternating "strong" and "weak" muscular movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirstein_4_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kirstein_4-20">[19]</a></sup> Given this alternation of left-right, of forward-backward and rise-fall, along with the <a href="/wiki/Symmetry_in_biology" title="Symmetry in biology">bilateral symmetry</a> of the human body, it is natural that many dances and much music are in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duple_and_quadruple_meter" title="Duple and quadruple meter">duple and quadruple meter</a>. Since some such movements require more time in one phase than the other – such as the longer time required to lift a hammer than to strike – some dance rhythms fall equally naturally into <a href="/wiki/Triple_metre" title="Triple metre">triple metre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Occasionally, as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_of_Southeastern_Europe" title="Music of Southeastern Europe">the folk dances of the Balkans</a>, dance traditions depend heavily on more complex rhythms. Further, complex dances composed of a fixed sequence of steps always require phrases and melodies of a certain fixed length to accompany that sequence.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_(painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901,_before_p.107).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="936" data-file-width="529" decoding="async" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg/130px-Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg/195px-Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg/260px-Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_%28painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901%2C_before_p.107%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lululaund_-_The_Dancing_Girl_(painting_and_silk_cloth._A.L._Baldry_1901,_before_p.107).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Lululaund – The Dancing Girl</i> (painting and silk cloth. A.L. Baldry 1901, before p. 107), The inscription reads; "Dancing is a form of rhythm/ Rhythm is a form of music/ Music is a form of thought/ And thought is a form of divinity."</div></div></div>
<p>The very act of dancing, the steps themselves, generate an "initial skeleton of rhythmic beats" that must have preceded any separate musical accompaniment, while dance itself, as much as music, requires time-keeping<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> just as utilitarian repetitive movements such as walking, hauling and digging take on, as they become refined, something of the quality of dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirstein_4_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kirstein_4-20">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>Musical accompaniment, therefore, arose in the earliest dance, so that ancient Egyptians attributed the origin of the dance to the divine Athotus, who was said to have observed that music accompanying religious rituals caused participants to move rhythmically and to have brought these movements into proportional measure. The same idea, that dance arises from musical rhythm, is still found in <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">renaissance</a> Europe in the works of the dancing master <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Ebreo_da_Pesaro" title="Guglielmo Ebreo da Pesaro">Guglielmo Ebreo da Pesaro</a> who speaks of dance as a physical movement that arises from and expresses inward, spiritual motion agreeing with the "measures and perfect concords of harmony" that fall upon the human ear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kirstein_4_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kirstein_4-20">[19]</a></sup> while, earlier, <a href="/wiki/Mechthild_of_Magdeburg" title="Mechthild of Magdeburg">Mechthild of Magdeburg</a>, seizing upon dance as a symbol of the holy life foreshadowed in Jesus' saying "I have piped and ye have not danced",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> writes;
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I can not dance unless thou leadest. If thou wouldst have me spring aloft, sing thou and I will spring, into love and from love to knowledge and from knowledge to ecstasy above all human sense<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thoinot_Arbeau" title="Thoinot Arbeau">Thoinot Arbeau</a>'s celebrated 16th-century dance-treatise <i>Orchésographie</i>, indeed, begins with definitions of over eighty distinct drum-rhythms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_with_Helen_Moller;_her_own_statement_of_her_philosophy_and_practice_and_teaching_formed_upon_the_classic_Greek_model,_and_adapted_to_meet_the_aesthetic_and_hygienic_needs_of_to-day,_with_(14784705065).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2090" data-file-width="1486" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Dancing_with_Helen_Moller%3B_her_own_statement_of_her_philosophy_and_practice_and_teaching_formed_upon_the_classic_Greek_model%2C_and_adapted_to_meet_the_aesthetic_and_hygienic_needs_of_to-day%2C_with_%2814784705065%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Dancing_with_Helen_Moller%3B_her_own_statement_of_her_philosophy_and_practice_and_teaching_formed_upon_the_classic_Greek_model%2C_and_adapted_to_meet_the_aesthetic_and_hygienic_needs_of_to-day%2C_with_%2814784705065%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Dancing_with_Helen_Moller%3B_her_own_statement_of_her_philosophy_and_practice_and_teaching_formed_upon_the_classic_Greek_model%2C_and_adapted_to_meet_the_aesthetic_and_hygienic_needs_of_to-day%2C_with_%2814784705065%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dancing_with_Helen_Moller;_her_own_statement_of_her_philosophy_and_practice_and_teaching_formed_upon_the_classic_Greek_model,_and_adapted_to_meet_the_aesthetic_and_hygienic_needs_of_to-day,_with_(14784705065).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Helen Moller</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Valse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1759" data-file-width="1181" decoding="async" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/La_Valse.jpg/220px-La_Valse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/La_Valse.jpg/330px-La_Valse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/La_Valse.jpg/440px-La_Valse.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Valse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Waltz_(Claudel)" title="The Waltz (Claudel)">The Waltz</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Camille_Claudel" title="Camille Claudel">Camille Claudel</a>, 1905 cast</div></div></div>
<p>As has been shown above, dance has been represented through the ages as having emerged as a response to music yet, as <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Kirstein" title="Lincoln Kirstein">Lincoln Kirstein</a> implied, it is at least as likely that primitive music arose from dance. Shawn concurs, stating that dance "was the first art of the human race, and the matrix out of which all other arts grew" and that even the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meter_(poetry)" title="Meter (poetry)">metre</a> in our poetry today is a result of the accents necessitated by body movement, as the dancing and reciting was performed simultaneously"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shawn_50_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shawn_50-18">[17]</a></sup> – an assertion somewhat supported by the common use of the term "foot" to describe the fundamental rhythmic units of poetry.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Percy_Scholes" title="Percy Scholes">Scholes</a>, not a dancer but a musician, offers support for this view, stating that the steady measures of music, of two, three or four beats to the bar, its equal and balanced phrases, regular cadences, contrasts and repetitions, may all be attributed to the "incalculable" influence of dance upon music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Jaques-Dalcroze" title="Émile Jaques-Dalcroze">Émile Jaques-Dalcroze</a>, primarily a musician and teacher, relates how a study of the physical movements of pianists led him "to the discovery that musical sensations of a rhythmic nature call for the muscular and nervous response of the whole organism", to develop "a special training designed to regulate nervous reactions and effect a co-ordination of muscles and nerves" and ultimately to seek the connections between "the art of music and the art of dance", which he formulated into his system of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalcroze_Eurhythmics" title="Dalcroze Eurhythmics">eurhythmics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> He concluded that "musical rhythm is only the transposition into sound of movements and dynamisms spontaneously and involuntarily expressing emotion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hence, though doubtless, as Shawn asserts, "it is quite possible to develop the dance without music and... music is perfectly capable of standing on its own feet without any assistance from the dance", nevertheless the "two arts will always be related and the relationship can be profitable both to the dance and to music",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> the precedence of one art over the other being a moot point. The <a href="/wiki/Common_metre" title="Common metre">common ballad measures</a> of hymns and folk-songs takes their name from dance, as does the <a href="/wiki/Carol_(music)" title="Carol (music)">carol</a>, originally a <a href="/wiki/Circle_dance" title="Circle dance">circle dance</a>. Many purely musical pieces have been named "<a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Minuet" title="Minuet">minuet</a>", for example, while many <a href="/wiki/Concert_dance" title="Concert dance">concert dances</a> have been produced that are based upon abstract musical pieces, such as <i><a href="/wiki/2_and_3_Part_Inventions" title="2 and 3 Part Inventions">2 and 3 Part Inventions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adams_Violin_Concerto" title="Adams Violin Concerto">Adams Violin Concerto</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Andantino_(ballet)" title="Andantino (ballet)">Andantino</a></i>. Similarly, poems are often structured and named after dances or musical works, while dance and music have both drawn their conception of "measure" or "metre" from poetry.
</p><p>Shawn quotes with approval the statement of Dalcroze that, while the art of musical rhythm consists in differentiating and combining time durations, pauses and accents "according to physiological law", that of "plastic rhythm" (i.e. dance) "is to designate movement in space, to interpret long time-values by slow movements and short ones by quick movements, regulate pauses by their divers successions and express sound accentuations in their multiple nuances by additions of bodily weight, by means of muscular innervations".
</p><p>Shawn nevertheless points out that the system of musical time is a "man-made, artificial thing.... a manufactured tool, whereas rhythm is something that has always existed and depends on man not at all", being "the continuous flowing time which our human minds cut up into convenient units", suggesting that music might be revivified by a return to the values and the time-perception of dancing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>The early-20th-century American dancer Helen Moller stated simply that "it is rhythm and form more than harmony and color which, from the beginning, has bound music, poetry and dancing together in a union that is indissoluble."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Approaches">Approaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Approaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dinastia_tang,_due_danzatrici,_cina_del_nord,_650_ca..JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1323" data-file-width="2692" decoding="async" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG/220px-Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG/330px-Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG/440px-Dinastia_tang%2C_due_danzatrici%2C_cina_del_nord%2C_650_ca..JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dinastia_tang,_due_danzatrici,_cina_del_nord,_650_ca..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> female dancers</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical">Theatrical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Theatrical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Concert dance, like <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, generally depends for its large-scale form upon a <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">narrative</a> <a href="/wiki/Dramatic_structure" title="Dramatic structure">dramatic structure</a>. The movements and gestures of the <a href="/wiki/Choreography" title="Choreography">choreography</a> are primarily intended to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mime" title="Mime">mime</a> the personality and aims of the characters and their part in the plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Such theatrical requirements tend towards longer, freer movements than those usual in non-narrative dance styles. On the other hand, the <i><a href="/wiki/Ballet_blanc" title="Ballet blanc">ballet blanc</a></i>, developed in the 19th century, allows interludes of rhythmic dance that developed into entirely "plotless" ballets in the 20th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> and that allowed fast, rhythmic dance-steps such as those of the <i>petit allegro</i>. A well-known example is <i><a href="/wiki/Danse_des_petits_cygnes" title="Danse des petits cygnes">The Cygnets' Dance</a></i> in act two of <i><a href="/wiki/Swan_Lake" title="Swan Lake">Swan Lake</a></i>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a> developed out of courtly dramatic productions of 16th- and 17th-century France and Italy and for some time dancers performed dances developed from those familiar from the musical suite,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> all of which were defined by definite rhythms closely identified with each dance. These appeared as <a href="/wiki/Character_dance" title="Character dance">character dances</a> in the era of <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">romantic nationalism</a>.
</p><p>Ballet reached widespread vogue in the romantic era, accompanied by a larger orchestra and grander musical conceptions that did not lend themselves easily to rhythmic clarity and by dance that emphasised dramatic mime. A broader concept of rhythm was needed, that which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rudolf_Laban" title="Rudolf Laban">Rudolf Laban</a> terms the "rhythm and shape" of movement that communicates character, emotion and intention,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> while only certain scenes required the exact synchronisation of step and music essential to other dance styles, so that, to Laban, modern Europeans seemed totally unable to grasp the meaning of "primitive rhythmic movements",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> a situation that began to change in the 20th century with such productions as <a href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky" title="Igor Stravinsky">Igor Stravinsky</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rite_of_Spring" title="The Rite of Spring">The Rite of Spring</a></i> with its new rhythmic language evoking primal feelings of a primitive past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indian classical dance styles, like ballet, are often in dramatic form, so that there is a similar complementarity between narrative expression and "pure" dance. In this case, the two are separately defined, though not always separately performed. The rhythmic elements, which are abstract and technical, are known as <i>nritta</i>. Both this and expressive dance <i>(nritya)</i>, though, are closely tied to the rhythmic system (<i><a href="/wiki/Tala_(music)" title="Tala (music)">tala</a></i>). Teachers have adapted the spoken rhythmic mnemonic system called <i><a href="/wiki/Bol_(music)" title="Bol (music)">bol</a></i> to the needs of dancers.
</p><p>Japanese classical dance-theatre styles such as <a href="/wiki/Kabuki" title="Kabuki">Kabuki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noh" title="Noh">Noh</a>, like Indian dance-drama, distinguish between narrative and abstract dance productions. The three main categories of kabuki are <i><a href="/wiki/Jidaimono" title="Jidaimono">jidaimono</a></i> (historical), <i><a href="/wiki/Sewamono" title="Sewamono">sewamono</a></i> (domestic) and <i><a href="/wiki/Shosagoto" title="Shosagoto">shosagoto</a></i> (dance pieces).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kabuki_MIT_Global_Shakespeares_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kabuki_MIT_Global_Shakespeares-38">[37]</a></sup> Somewhat similarly, Noh distinguishes between <i>Geki Noh</i>, based around the advancement of plot and the narration of action, and <i>Furyū Noh</i>, dance pieces involving acrobatics, stage properties, multiple characters and elaborate stage action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ortolani_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ortolani-39">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Participatory_and_social">Participatory and social</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Participatory and social">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dela_Says_Yippee_at_YDW_2019.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Contra_dance" title="Contra dance">contra dance</a>, a form of participatory social folk dance with mixed European roots</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_dances" title="Social dances">Social dances</a>, those intended for participation rather than for an audience, may include various forms of mime and narrative, but are typically set much more closely to the rhythmic pattern of music, so that terms like <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">polka</a> refer as much to musical pieces as to the dance itself. The rhythm of the dancers' feet may even form an essential part of the music, as in <a href="/wiki/Tap_dance" title="Tap dance">tap dance</a>. African dance, for example, is rooted in fixed basic steps, but may also allow a high degree of rhythmic interpretation: the feet or the trunk mark the basic pulse while cross-rhythms are picked up by shoulders, knees, or head, with the best dancers simultaneously giving plastic expression to all the elements of the <a href="/wiki/Polyrhythm" title="Polyrhythm">polyrhythmic</a> pattern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_traditions">Cultural traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cultural traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_(7269658432).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2267" data-file-width="3480" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/290px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/435px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/580px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_(7269658432).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Ugandan</a> youth dance at a cultural celebration of peace</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_dance" title="African dance">African dance</a></div>
<p>Dance in Africa is deeply integrated into society and major events in a community are frequently reflected in dances: dances are performed for births and funerals, weddings and wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WelshHanley2010_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-WelshHanley2010-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 13">: 13 </span></sup> Traditional dances impart cultural morals, including religious traditions and sexual standards; give vent to repressed emotions, such as <a href="/wiki/Grief" title="Grief">grief</a>; motivate community members to cooperate, whether fighting wars or grinding grain; enact spiritual rituals; and contribute to <a href="/wiki/Structural_cohesion" title="Structural cohesion">social cohesiveness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanna1973_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hanna1973-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thousands of dances are performed around the continent. These may be divided into traditional, neotraditional, and classical styles: <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folkloric</a> dances of a particular society, dances created more recently in imitation of traditional styles, and dances transmitted more formally in schools or private lessons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WelshHanley2010_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-WelshHanley2010-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 18">: 18 </span></sup> African dance has been altered by many forces, such as European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Missionaries" title="Missionaries">missionaries</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonialist" title="Colonialist">colonialist</a> governments, who often suppressed local dance traditions as licentious or distracting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanna1973_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hanna1973-42">[41]</a></sup> Dance in contemporary African cultures still serves its traditional functions in new contexts; dance may celebrate the inauguration of a hospital, build community for rural migrants in unfamiliar cities, and be incorporated into Christian church ceremonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanna1973_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hanna1973-42">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_dance#Asia" title="History of dance">History of dance § Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nandini_Ghosal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="948" data-file-width="636" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Nandini_Ghosal.jpg/170px-Nandini_Ghosal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Nandini_Ghosal.jpg/255px-Nandini_Ghosal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Nandini_Ghosal.jpg/340px-Nandini_Ghosal.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nandini_Ghosal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Indian classical dancer</div></div></div>

codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mintha_Theater_2.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the Mintha Theater (<a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>) a master teacher of the Inwa School of Performing Arts demonstrates traditional hand movements.</div></div></div>
<p>All <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Indian_dance" title="Classical Indian dance">Indian classical dances</a> are to varying degrees rooted in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natyashastra" title="Natyashastra">Natyashastra</a></i> and therefore share common features: for example, the <i>mudra</i>s (hand positions), some body positions, leg movement and the inclusion of dramatic or expressive acting or <a href="/wiki/Abhinaya" title="Abhinaya">abhinaya</a>. Indian classical music provides accompaniment and dancers of nearly all the styles wear bells around their ankles to counterpoint and complement the percussion.
</p><p>There are now many regional varieties of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_dance" title="Indian classical dance">Indian classical dance</a>. Dances like <i>"Odra Magadhi"</i>, which after decades-long debate, has been traced to present day Mithila, <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a> region's dance form of <a href="/wiki/Odissi" title="Odissi">Odissi</a> (Orissi), indicate influence of dances in cultural interactions between different regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab</a> area overlapping India and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> is the place of origin of <a href="/wiki/Bhangra_(dance)" title="Bhangra (dance)">Bhangra</a>. It is widely known both as a style of music and a dance. It is mostly related to ancient harvest celebrations, love, patriotism or social issues. Its music is coordinated by a musical instrument called the 'Dhol'. Bhangra is not just music but a dance, a celebration of the harvest where people beat the dhol (drum), sing Boliyaan (lyrics) and dance. It developed further with the Vaisakhi festival of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dances_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Dances of Sri Lanka">dances of Sri Lanka</a> include the devil dances (<i>yakun natima</i>), a carefully crafted ritual reaching far back into Sri Lanka's pre-Buddhist past that combines ancient "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ayurvedic" title="Ayurvedic">Ayurvedic</a>" concepts of disease causation with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological_manipulation" title="Psychological manipulation">psychological manipulation</a> and combines many aspects including Sinhalese cosmology. Their influence can be seen on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_dances_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Classical dances of Sri Lanka">classical dances of Sri Lanka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3504" data-file-width="2336" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg/220px-Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg/330px-Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg/440px-Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bali-Danse_0729a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Balinese_dance" title="Balinese dance">Balinese dancer</a></div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dances_in_Indonesia" title="Dances in Indonesia">Indonesian dances</a> reflect the richness and diversity of Indonesian ethnic groups and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Indonesia" title="Culture of Indonesia">cultures</a>. There are more than 1,300 <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">ethnic groups in Indonesia</a>, it can be seen from the cultural roots of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melanesian_peoples" title="Melanesian peoples">Melanesian peoples</a>, and various cultural influences from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and the west. Dances in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> originate from ritual movements and religious ceremonies, this kind of dance usually begins with rituals, such as war dances, shaman dances to cure or ward off disease, dances to call rain and other types of dances. With the acceptance of dharma religion in the 1st century in Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> rituals were celebrated in various artistic performances. Hindu epics such as the <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a> and also the <a href="/wiki/Panji_tales" title="Panji tales">Panji</a> became the inspiration to be shown in a dance-drama called "Sendratari" resembling "<a href="/wiki/Ramayana_Ballet" title="Ramayana Ballet">ballet</a>" in the western tradition. An elaborate and highly stylized dance method was invented and has survived to this day, especially on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>. The Javanese <a href="/wiki/Wayang_wong" title="Wayang wong">Wayang wong</a> dance takes footage from the Ramayana or Mahabharata episodes, but this dance is very different from the Indian version, indonesian dances do not pay as much attention to the "<a href="/wiki/Mudra" title="Mudra">mudras</a>" as Indian dances: even more to show local forms. The sacred <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> ritual dance <a href="/wiki/Bedhaya" title="Bedhaya">Bedhaya</a> is believed to date back to the <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> period in the 14th century or even earlier, this dance originated from ritual dances performed by virgin girls to worship Hindu Gods such as <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brahma" title="Brahma">Brahma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>. In Bali, dance has become an integral part of the sacred Hindu Dharma rituals. Some experts believe that <a href="/wiki/Balinese_dance" title="Balinese dance">Balinese dance</a> comes from an older dance tradition from Java. Reliefs from temples in <a href="/wiki/East_Java" title="East Java">East Java</a> from the 14th century feature crowns and headdresses similar to the headdresses used in Balinese dance today. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> began to spread to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_archipelago" title="Indonesian archipelago">Indonesian archipelago</a> when indigenous dances and dharma dances were still popular. Artists and dancers still use styles from the previous era, replacing stories with more Islamic interpretations and clothing that is more closed according to Islamic teachings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Folk_Dances_Indonesia_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Folk_Dances_Indonesia-46">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_dance" title="Middle Eastern dance">dances of the Middle East</a> are usually the traditional forms of <a href="/wiki/Circle_dance" title="Circle dance">circle dancing</a> which are modernized to an extent. They would include <a href="/wiki/Dabke" title="Dabke">dabke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamzara" title="Tamzara">tamzara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_folk_dance" title="Assyrian folk dance">Assyrian folk dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_dance" title="Kurdish dance">Kurdish dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_dance" title="Armenian dance">Armenian dance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_dance" title="Turkish dance">Turkish dance</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Badley_2000._pp_391-395_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Badley_2000._pp_391-395-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> All these forms of dances would usually involve participants engaging each other by holding hands or arms (depending on the style of the dance). They would make rhythmic moves with their legs and shoulders as they curve around the dance floor. The head of the dance would generally hold a <a href="/wiki/Walking_stick" title="Walking stick">cane</a> or <a href="/wiki/Handkerchief" title="Handkerchief">handkerchief</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Badley_2000._pp_391-395_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Badley_2000._pp_391-395-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_and_North_America">Europe and North America<span class="anchor" id="Europe"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Europe and North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Concert_dance" title="Concert dance">Concert dance</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_dance#Europe" title="History of dance">History of dance § Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dance-At-Bougival.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4366" data-file-width="2301" decoding="async" height="323" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dance-At-Bougival.jpg/170px-Dance-At-Bougival.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dance-At-Bougival.jpg/255px-Dance-At-Bougival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Dance-At-Bougival.jpg/340px-Dance-At-Bougival.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dance-At-Bougival.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Dance_at_Bougival" title="Dance at Bougival">Dance at Bougival</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Auguste_Renoir" title="Pierre-Auguste Renoir">Pierre-Auguste Renoir</a> (1883)</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">Folk dances</a> vary across Europe and may date back hundreds or thousands of years, but many have features in common such as <a href="/wiki/Group_dance" title="Group dance">group participation</a> led by a <a href="/wiki/Caller_(dancing)" title="Caller (dancing)">caller</a>, hand-holding or arm-linking between participants, and fixed musical forms known as caroles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lee_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-lee-50">[49]</a></sup> Some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Maypole" title="Maypole">maypole</a> dance are common to many nations, while others such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A9ilidh" title="Céilidh">céilidh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">polka</a> are deeply-rooted in a single culture. Some European folk dances such as the <a href="/wiki/Square_dance" title="Square dance">square dance</a> were brought to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> and subsequently became part of American culture.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1425" data-file-width="1210" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG/220px-NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG/330px-NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG/440px-NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NutcrackerSnowPas.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two classical ballet dancers perform a sequence of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nutcracker" title="The Nutcracker">The Nutcracker</a></i>, one of the best known works of classical dance.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="18" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Sioux_buffalo_dance,_1894.ogv" height="165" id="mwe_player_3" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv/220px--Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="256224" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b3/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="1535722" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file, 320 × 240 (1.54 Mbps)" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv" type='video/ogg; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="130864" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="160" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b3/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv/Sioux_buffalo_dance%2C_1894.ogv.160p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sioux_buffalo_dance,_1894.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sioux <i><a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Dance_(film)" title="Buffalo Dance (film)">Buffalo Dance</a></i>, 1894</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">Ballet</a> developed first in Italy and then in France from lavish court spectacles that combined music, drama, poetry, song, costumes and dance. Members of the court nobility took part as performers. During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, himself a dancer, dance became more codified. Professional dancers began to take the place of court amateurs, and ballet masters were licensed by the French government. The first ballet dance academy was the Académie Royale de Danse (Royal Dance Academy), opened in Paris in 1661. Shortly thereafter, the first institutionalized ballet troupe, associated with the Academy, was formed; this troupe began as an all-male ensemble but by 1681 opened to include women as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lecomte_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-lecomte-8">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/20th_century_concert_dance" title="20th century concert dance">20th century concert dance</a> brought an explosion of innovation in dance style characterized by an exploration of freer technique. Early pioneers of what became known as <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern dance</a> include <a href="/wiki/Loie_Fuller" title="Loie Fuller">Loie Fuller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isadora_Duncan" title="Isadora Duncan">Isadora Duncan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Wigman" title="Mary Wigman">Mary Wigman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_St._Denis" title="Ruth St. Denis">Ruth St. Denis</a>. The relationship of music to dance serves as the basis for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurhythmics" title="Eurhythmics">Eurhythmics</a>, devised by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emile_Jaques-Dalcroze" title="Emile Jaques-Dalcroze">Emile Jaques-Dalcroze</a>, which was influential to the development of Modern dance and modern ballet through artists such as <a href="/wiki/Marie_Rambert" title="Marie Rambert">Marie Rambert</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eurythmy" title="Eurythmy">Eurythmy</a>, developed by <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Steiner" title="Rudolf Steiner">Rudolf Steiner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marie_Steiner-von_Sivers" title="Marie Steiner-von Sivers">Marie Steiner-von Sivers</a>, combines formal elements reminiscent of traditional dance with the new freer style, and introduced a complex new vocabulary to dance. In the 1920s, important founders of the new style such as <a href="/wiki/Martha_Graham" title="Martha Graham">Martha Graham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doris_Humphrey" title="Doris Humphrey">Doris Humphrey</a> began their work. Since this time, a wide variety of dance styles have been developed; see <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">Modern dance</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_dance" title="African American dance">African American dance</a> developed in everyday spaces, rather than in dance studios, schools or companies. <a href="/wiki/Tap_dance" title="Tap dance">Tap dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz_dance" title="Jazz dance">jazz dance</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swing_dance" title="Swing dance">swing dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_dance" title="Hip hop dance">hip hop dance</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lindy_hop" title="Lindy hop">lindy hop</a> with its relationship to <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll music</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll_(dance)" title="Rock and roll (dance)">rock and roll dance</a> have had a global influence. Dance styles fusing classical ballet technique with African-American dance have also appeared in the 21st century, including <a href="/wiki/Hiplet_(dance_style)" title="Hiplet (dance style)">Hiplet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kourlas_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-kourlas-51">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_dance" title="Latin American dance">Latin American dance</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="180"
