srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG/360px-HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG/480px-HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HK_TST_night_%E6%9F%8F%E9%BA%97%E8%B3%BC%E7%89%A9%E5%A4%A7%E9%81%93_Park_Lane_Shopper%27s_Boulevard_%E5%B7%B4%E8%A5%BF_Brasil_%E6%A3%AE%E5%B7%B4%E8%88%9E%E5%A8%98_Samba_female_dancers_Nov-2010_02.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samba_school" title="Samba school">Street samba</a> dancers perform in carnival parades and contests.</div></div></div>
<p>Dance is central to <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> social life and culture. Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Samba_(Brazilian_dance)" title="Samba (Brazilian dance)">Samba</a>, Argentinian <a href="/wiki/Tango" title="Tango">tango</a>, and Cuban <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">salsa</a> are internationally popular partner dances, and other national dances—<a href="/wiki/Merengue_(dance)" title="Merengue (dance)">merengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cueca" title="Cueca">cueca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">plena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jarabe" title="Jarabe">jarabe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joropo" title="Joropo">joropo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marinera" title="Marinera">marinera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumbia" title="Cumbia">cumbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(dance)" title="Bachata (dance)">bachata</a> and others—are important components of their respective countries' cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chasteen2004_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chasteen2004-52">[51]</a></sup> Traditional <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> festivals incorporate these and other dances in enormous celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MusmonHanley2010_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-MusmonHanley2010-53">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Dance has played an important role in forging a collective identity among the many cultural and ethnic groups of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DelgadoMuñoz1997_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-DelgadoMuñoz1997-54">[53]</a></sup> Dance served to unite the many African, European, and indigenous peoples of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chasteen2004_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chasteen2004-52">[51]</a></sup> Certain dance genres, such as <a href="/wiki/Capoeira" title="Capoeira">capoeira</a>, and body movements, especially the characteristic <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Quebrada_(dance)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quebrada (dance) (page does not exist)">quebradas</a></i> or <a href="/wiki/Pelvis" title="Pelvis">pelvis</a> swings, have been variously banned and celebrated throughout Latin American history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DelgadoMuñoz1997_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-DelgadoMuñoz1997-54">[53]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dance studies are offered through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arts" title="Arts">arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> programs of many higher education institutions. Some universities offer <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> and higher <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">academic degrees</a> in Dance. A dance study curriculum may encompass a diverse range of courses and topics, including dance practice and performance, choreography, <a href="/wiki/Ethnochoreology" title="Ethnochoreology">ethnochoreology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kinesiology" title="Kinesiology">kinesiology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_notation" title="Dance notation">dance notation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dance_therapy" title="Dance therapy">dance therapy</a>. Most recently, dance and movement therapy has been integrated in some schools into math lessons for students with learning disabilities, emotional/behavioral disabilities and/or attention deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibney_Dance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gibney_Dance.jpg/280px-Gibney_Dance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gibney_Dance.jpg/420px-Gibney_Dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gibney_Dance.jpg/560px-Gibney_Dance.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibney_Dance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A dancer practices in a <a href="/wiki/Dance_studio" title="Dance studio">dance studio</a>, the primary setting for training in classical dance and many other styles.</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupations">Occupations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Occupations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_dance_occupations" title="List of dance occupations">List of dance occupations</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dancers">Dancers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dancers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Professional dancers are usually employed on contract or for particular performances or productions. The professional life of a dancer is generally one of constantly changing work situations, strong competitive pressure and low pay. Consequently, professional dancers often must supplement their incomes to achieve financial stability. In the U.S. many professional dancers belong to unions (such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Guild_of_Musical_Artists" title="American Guild of Musical Artists">American Guild of Musical Artists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> and <a href="/wiki/Actors%27_Equity_Association" title="Actors' Equity Association">Actors' Equity Association</a>) that establish working conditions and minimum salaries for their members. Professional dancers must possess large amounts of athleticism. To lead a successful career, it is advantageous to be versatile in many styles of dance, have a strong technical background and to utilize other forms of physical training to remain fit and healthy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teachers">Teachers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Teachers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dance teachers typically focus on teaching dance performance, or coaching competitive dancers, or both. They typically have performance experience in the types of dance they teach or coach. For example, <a href="/wiki/Dancesport" title="Dancesport">dancesport</a> teachers and coaches are often tournament dancers or former dancesport performers. Dance teachers may be self-employed, or employed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dance_school" title="Dance school">dance schools</a> or general education institutions with dance programs. Some work for university programs or other schools that are associated with professional classical dance (e.g., ballet) or modern dance companies. Others are employed by smaller, privately owned dance schools that offer dance training and performance coaching for various types of dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Choreographers">Choreographers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Choreographers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Choreography_(dance)" title="Choreography (dance)">Choreographers</a> are the ones that design the dancing movements within a dance, they are often university trained and are typically employed for particular projects or, more rarely may work on contract as the resident choreographer for a specific dance company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitions">Competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1033" data-file-width="1793" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg/320px-MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg/480px-MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg/640px-MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MIT_2006_Standard_Prechamp_Final_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An amateur dancesport competition, featuring the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viennese_Waltz" title="Viennese Waltz">Viennese Waltz</a></div></div></div>
<p>A <b>dance competition</b> is an organized event in which contestants perform dances before a judge or judges for awards, and in some cases, monetary prizes. There are several major types of dance competitions, distinguished primarily by the style or styles of dances performed. Major types of dance competitions include:
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Dancesport" title="Dancesport">Dancesport</a></b>, which is focused exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Ballroom_dance" title="Ballroom dance">ballroom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_dance" title="Latin dance">latin dance</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Competitive_dance" title="Competitive dance">Competitive dance</a></b>, in which a variety of theater dance styles, such as <a href="/wiki/Acro_dance" title="Acro dance">acrobatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz_dance" title="Jazz dance">jazz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip-hop" title="Hip-hop">hip-hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyrical_dance" title="Lyrical dance">lyrical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Step_dance" title="Step dance">stepping</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tap_dance" title="Tap dance">tap</a>, are permitted.</li>
<li><b>Single-style</b> competitions, such as; <a href="/wiki/Scottish_highland_dance" title="Scottish highland dance">highland dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_squad" title="Dance squad">dance team</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Irish_dance" title="Irish dance">Irish dance</a>, that only permit a single dance style.</li>
<li><b>Open</b> competitions, that permit a wide variety of dance styles.  An example of this is the TV program <i><a href="/wiki/So_You_Think_You_Can_Dance" title="So You Think You Can Dance">So You Think You Can Dance</a></i>.</li>
<li><b>Olympic</b>, Dance has been trying to be part of the Olympic sport since 1930s.</li></ul>
<p>In addition, there are numerous dance competitions shows <a href="/wiki/Dance_on_television" title="Dance on television">presented on television</a> and other mass media.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p><br/>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Many definitions of dance have been proposed. This definition is based on the following:<br/><br/>
"Dance is human movement created and expressed for an aesthetic purpose."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fraleigh1987_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fraleigh1987-1">[1]</a></sup><br/><br/>
"Dance is a transient mode of expression performed in a given form and style by the human body moving in space. Dance occurs through purposefully selected and controlled rhythmic movements; the resulting phenomenon is recognized as dance both by the performer and the observing members of a given group."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><br/><br/>
"Dance is human behaviour composed (from the dancer’s perspective, which is usually shared by the audience members of the dancer’s culture) of purposeful (individual choice and social learning play a role), intentionally rhythmical, and culturally patterned sequences of nonverbal body movement mostly other than those performed in ordinary motor activities. The motion (in time, space, and with effort) has an inherent and aesthetic value (the notion of appropriateness and competency as viewed by the dancer’s culture) and symbolic potential."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
